style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; background: transparent; text-align: left; padding-left: 5px; padding-top: 3px">\n           <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n            Astronauts\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n           <ul>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">\n              The Mercury Seven\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apollo_astronauts" title="List of Apollo astronauts">\n              Gemini/Apollo astronauts\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li>\n             <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Corps" title="NASA Astronaut Corps">\n              NASA Astronaut Corps\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:United_States_space_program_sidebar" title="Template:United States space program sidebar">\n             <abbr title="View this template">\n              v\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:United_States_space_program_sidebar" title="Template talk:United States space program sidebar">\n             <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n              t\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:United_States_space_program_sidebar&amp;action=edit">\n             <abbr title="Edit this template">\n              e\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg/220px-Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg/330px-Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg/440px-Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_delivers_ISS_P1_truss.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n          Endeavour\n         </a>\n         \' in orbit, 2002\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_Patch.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="296" data-file-width="285" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Shuttle_Patch.svg/150px-Shuttle_Patch.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Shuttle_Patch.svg/225px-Shuttle_Patch.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Shuttle_Patch.svg/300px-Shuttle_Patch.svg.png 2x" width="150"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_Patch.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Patch\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </b>\n       was the United States government\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        manned\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       program, administered by\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       from 1972 to 2011 and first flown in 1981. Its official name,\n       <i>\n        Space Transportation System (STS)\n       </i>\n       , was taken from a 1969 plan for\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Transportation_System" title="Space Transportation System">\n        a system of reusable spacecraft\n       </a>\n       of which it was the only item funded for development.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94composed of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_orbiter" title="Space Shuttle orbiter">\n        orbiter\n       </a>\n       launched with two reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        solid rocket boosters\n       </a>\n       and a disposable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external fuel tank\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94carried up to eight\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">\n        astronauts\n       </a>\n       and up to 50,000\xc2\xa0lb (23,000\xc2\xa0kg) of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" title="Payload (air and space craft)">\n        payload\n       </a>\n       into\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       (LEO). When its mission was complete, the orbiter would\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_reentry" title="Atmospheric reentry">\n        re-enter\n       </a>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s atmosphere and land like a\n       <a href="/wiki/Glider_(aircraft)" title="Glider (aircraft)">\n        glider\n       </a>\n       at either the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n        Edwards Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Shuttle is the only winged manned spacecraft to have achieved orbit and landing, and the only reusable manned space vehicle that has ever made multiple flights into orbit (the Russian shuttle\n       <a href="/wiki/Buran_(spacecraft)" title="Buran (spacecraft)">\n        Buran\n       </a>\n       was very similar and was designed to have the same capabilities but made only one unmanned spaceflight before it was cancelled). Its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_space_shuttle_missions" title="List of space shuttle missions">\n        missions\n       </a>\n       involved carrying large payloads to various orbits (including segments to be added to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS)), providing crew rotation for the space station, and performing service missions. The orbiter also recovered\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">\n        satellites\n       </a>\n       and other payloads (e.g., from the ISS) from orbit and returned them to Earth, though its use in this capacity was rare. Each vehicle was designed with a projected lifespan of 100 launches, or 10 years\' operational life, though original selling points on the shuttles were over 150 launches and over a 15-year operational span with a \'launch per month\' expected at the peak of the program, but extensive delays in the development of the International Space Station\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iss-casis.org_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iss-casis.org-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       never created such a peak demand for frequent flights.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the concept had been explored since the late 1960s, the program formally commenced in 1972, and was the sole focus of NASA\'s manned operations after the final\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       flights in the mid-1970s. The Shuttle was originally conceived of and presented to the public in 1972 as a \'Space Truck\' which would, among other things, be used to build a United States space station in\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       during the 1980s and then be replaced by a new vehicle by the early 1990s. The stalled plans for a U.S. space station evolved into the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       and were formally initiated in 1983 by U.S. President\n       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">\n        Ronald Reagan\n       </a>\n       , but the ISS suffered from long delays, design changes and cost over-runs\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iss-casis.org_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iss-casis.org-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and forced the service life of the Space Shuttle to be extended several times until 2011 when it was finally retired \xe2\x80\x93 serving twice as long than it was originally designed to do. In 2004, according to the President George W. Bush\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n        Vision for Space Exploration\n       </a>\n       , use of the Space Shuttle was to be focused almost exclusively on completing assembly of the ISS, which was far behind schedule at that point.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first experimental orbiter\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">\n        <i>\n         Enterprise\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       was a high-altitude glider, launched from the back of a specially modified Boeing 747, only for\n       <a href="/wiki/Approach_and_Landing_Tests" title="Approach and Landing Tests">\n        initial atmospheric landing tests (ALT)\n       </a>\n       .\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\'\n       </i>\n       s first test flight was on February 18, 1977, only five years after the Shuttle program was formally initiated; leading to the launch of the first space-worthy shuttle\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       on April 12, 1981 on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       . The Space Shuttle program finished with its last mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">\n        STS-135\n       </a>\n       flown by\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n        <i>\n         Atlantis\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , in July 2011, retiring the final Shuttle in the fleet. The Space Shuttle program formally ended on August 31, 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the Shuttle\'s retirement, many of its original duties are performed by an assortment of government and private vessels. The European ATV\n       <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       supplied the ISS between 2008 and 2015. Classified military missions are being flown by the US Air Force\'s unmanned\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_plane" title="Space plane">\n        space plane\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_X-37" title="Boeing X-37">\n        X-37B\n       </a>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       . By 2012, cargo to the International Space Station was already being delivered commercially under NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Resupply Services\n       </a>\n       by SpaceX\'s partially reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon spacecraft\n       </a>\n       , followed by Orbital Sciences\'\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">\n        Cygnus spacecraft\n       </a>\n       in late 2013. Crew service to the ISS is currently provided by the Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(spacecraft)" title="Soyuz (spacecraft)">\n        Soyuz\n       </a>\n       while work on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development program\n       </a>\n       proceeds. For missions beyond\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       , NASA is building the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" title="Orion spacecraft">\n        Orion spacecraft\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conception_and_development">\n        Conception and development\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_design_process" title="Space Shuttle design process">\n        Space Shuttle design process\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Nixon_and_James_Fletcher_Discuss_the_Space_Shuttle_-_GPN-2002-000109.jpg">\n         <img alt="" Fletcher">\n          Fletcher\n         </a>\n         in January 1972, three months before Congress approved funding for the Shuttle program\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Approach_and_Landing_Tests_crews.jpg">\n         <img alt="" <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Approach_and_Landing_Tests_crews.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Shuttle approach and landing test crews, 1976\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="2870" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg/220px-Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg/330px-Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg/440px-Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spacelab_Arrival_Ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center_-_GPN-2002-000088.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NASA Administrator address the crowd at the Spacelab arrival ceremony in February 1982. On the podium with him is then-Vice President George Bush, the director general of European Space Agency (ESA), Eric Quistgaard, and director of Kennedy Space Center Richard G. Smith\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n        Apollo 11\n       </a>\n       moon landing in 1969, NASA began early studies of space shuttle designs. In 1969, President\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Milhous_Nixon" title="Richard Milhous Nixon">\n        Richard Nixon\n       </a>\n       formed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Task_Group" title="Space Task Group">\n        Space Task Group\n       </a>\n       , chaired by Vice President\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiro_T._Agnew" title="Spiro T. Agnew">\n        Spiro T. Agnew\n       </a>\n       . This group outlined ambitious post-Apollo missions centered on a large permanently manned\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">\n        space station\n       </a>\n       , a small reusable logistics vehicle that would support it, and ultimately a manned mission to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       . Smaller goals included a variety of space vehicles for moving spacecraft around in\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decision_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-decision-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Presenting the plans to Nixon, Agnew was told that the administration would not commit to a Mars mission, and limited activity to low Earth orbit for the immediate future.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He was then told to select one of the two remaining proposals. After some debate between the station and the vehicle, the vehicle was chosen; suitably designed, such a spacecraft could perform some longer-duration missions and thus fill some of the goals of the station, and over the longer run, could help lower the cost of access to space and make the station less expensive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decision_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-decision-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The goal, as presented by NASA to Congress, was to provide a much less-expensive means of access to space that would be used by NASA, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       , and other commercial and scientific users.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During early shuttle development there was great debate about the optimal shuttle design that best balanced capability, development cost and operating cost. Ultimately the current design was chosen, using a reusable winged orbiter, reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        solid rocket boosters\n       </a>\n       , and an expendable\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external fuel tank\n       </a>\n       for the orbiter\'s main engines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decision_4-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-decision-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle program was formally launched on January 5, 1972, when President Nixon announced that NASA would proceed with the development of a reusable space shuttle system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decision_4-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-decision-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The stated goals of "transforming the space frontier...into familiar territory, easily accessible for human endeavor"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       was to be achieved by launching as many as 50 missions per year, with hopes of driving down per-mission costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_July_2011_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP_July_2011-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The prime contractor for the program was\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_Rockwell" title="North American Rockwell">\n        North American Rockwell\n       </a>\n       (later\n       <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_International" title="Rockwell International">\n        Rockwell International\n       </a>\n       , now\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       ), the same company responsible for building the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">\n        Apollo Command/Service Module\n       </a>\n       . The contractor for the Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Boosters was\n       <a href="/wiki/Thiokol" title="Thiokol">\n        Morton Thiokol\n       </a>\n       (now part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Alliant_Techsystems" title="Alliant Techsystems">\n        Alliant Techsystems\n       </a>\n       ), for the external tank,\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Marietta" title="Martin Marietta">\n        Martin Marietta\n       </a>\n       (now\n       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">\n        Lockheed Martin\n       </a>\n       ), and for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_main_engine" title="Space Shuttle main engine">\n        Space Shuttle main engines\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocketdyne" title="Rocketdyne">\n        Rocketdyne\n       </a>\n       (now\n       <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">\n        Pratt &amp; Whitney\n       </a>\n       Rocketdyne, part of\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Technologies" title="United Technologies">\n        United Technologies\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decision_4-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-decision-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first orbiter was originally planned to be named\n       <i>\n        Constitution\n       </i>\n       , but a massive write-in campaign from fans of the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">\n         Star Trek\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       television series convinced the White House to change the name to\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">\n         Enterprise\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orbiter_names_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-orbiter_names-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Amid great fanfare,\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       (designated OV-101) was rolled out on September 17, 1976, and later conducted a successful series of glide-approach and landing tests in 1977 that were the first real validation of the design.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tleft">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_concepts.jpg">\n            <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="390" height="216" concepts.\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tright">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Columbia_launching.jpg">\n            <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3000" height="185" The External Tank was painted white for the first two Space Shuttle launches. From\n            <a href="/wiki/STS-3" title="STS-3">\n             STS-3\n            </a>\n            on, it was left unpainted.\n            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n             [\n             <i>\n              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">\n                citation needed\n               </span>\n              </a>\n             </i>\n             ]\n            </sup>\n            . The first two missions had tanks painted white, this elimination saved some weight (about 600 lbs / 272 kg).\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_11-0">\n             <a href="#cite_note-space.com-11">\n              [11]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n            Decades later some questioned if the paint might have prevented the ice-soaked foam shedding issue that lead to the destruction of\n            <i>\n             Columbia\n            </i>\n            .\n            <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_11-1">\n             <a href="#cite_note-space.com-11">\n              [11]\n             </a>\n            </sup>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <div class="thumb tright">\n          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg">\n            <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3552" data-file-width="4620" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg/220px-Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg/440px-Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n           </a>\n           <div class="thumbcaption">\n            <div class="magnify">\n             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teleoperator_Retrieval_System_with_Shuttle.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n             </a>\n            </div>\n            It was hope the Shuttle might be able to rejuvenate Skylab but it was not ready in time\xe2\x80\x94higher than expected solar activity caused accelerated orbital decay\n           </div>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Program_history">\n        Program history\n Spacelab was a major European contribution to the Space Shuttle Program\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-61-A_compartment_trainer.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="441" data-file-width="631" height="154"  <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-61-A_compartment_trainer.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         European astronauts prepare for their Spacelab mission, 1984.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astro2_sts67_big.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         SpaceLab hardware included a pressurized lab, but also other equipment allowing the Orbiter to serve as a manned space observatory (\n         <i>\n          Astro-2\n         </i>\n         mission, 1995, shown)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       All Space Shuttle missions were launched from the Kennedy Space Center (KSC).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle_launch_commit_criteria" title="Space shuttle launch commit criteria">\n        weather criteria used for launch\n       </a>\n       included, but were not limited to: precipitation, temperatures, cloud cover, lightning forecast, wind, and humidity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather_launch_criteria_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-weather_launch_criteria-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Shuttle was not launched under conditions where it could have been struck by\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first fully functional orbiter was\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (designated OV-102), built in\n       <a href="/wiki/Palmdale,_California" title="Palmdale, California">\n        Palmdale, California\n       </a>\n       . It was delivered to\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       (KSC) on March 25, 1979, and was first launched on April 12, 1981\xe2\x80\x94the 20th anniversary of\n       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">\n        Yuri Gagarin\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">\n        space flight\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94with a crew of two.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n         Challenger\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (OV-099) was delivered to KSC in July 1982,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n         Discovery\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (OV-103) in November 1983,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n         Atlantis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (OV-104) in April 1985 and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         Endeavour\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in May 1991.\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       was originally built and used as a Structural Test Article (STA-099), but was converted to a complete orbiter when this was found to be less expensive than converting\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       from its Approach and Landing Test configuration into a spaceworthy vehicle.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On April 24, 1990,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       carried the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       into space during\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-31" title="STS-31">\n        STS-31\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the course of 135 missions flown, two orbiters (\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       ) suffered catastrophic accidents, with the loss of all crew members, totaling 14 astronauts.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The accidents led to national level inquiries and detailed analysis of why the accidents occurred.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-space.com-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There was a significant pause where changes were made before the Shuttles returned to flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_11-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-space.com-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Columbia disaster occurred in 2003, but STS took more than a year off before returning to flight in June 2005 with the STS-114 mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space.com_11-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-space.com-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The previous break was between January 1986 (when the Challenger disaster occurred) and 32 months later when\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-26" title="STS-26">\n        STS-26\n       </a>\n       was launched on September 29, 1988.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history.nasa.gov_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history.nasa.gov-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The longest Shuttle mission was\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-80" title="STS-80">\n        STS-80\n       </a>\n       lasting 17 days, 15 hours. The final flight of the Space Shuttle program was\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">\n        STS-135\n       </a>\n       on July 8, 2011.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accomplishments">\n        Accomplishments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Accomplishments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6048" data-file-width="4032" height="330" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg/330px-Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg/440px-Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Endeavour_docked_to_ISS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n         docked with the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n         (ISS), 2011\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Upgrading_Hubble_during_SM1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="992" height="169" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Upgrading_Hubble_during_SM1.jpg/340px-Upgrading_Hubble_during_SM1.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Upgrading_Hubble_during_SM1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Astronauts\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_D._Akers" title="Thomas D. Akers">\n          Thomas D. Akers\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_C._Thornton" title="Kathryn C. Thornton">\n          Kathryn C. Thornton\n         </a>\n         install corrective optics on the Hubble Space Telescope during\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-61" title="STS-61">\n          STS-61\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Space Shuttle missions have included:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">\n         Spacelab\n        </a>\n        missions\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA28_16-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-NASA28-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Including:\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          Science\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA28_16-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NASA28-16">\n            [16]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Astronomy\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA28_16-2">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NASA28-16">\n            [16]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Crystal growth\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA28_16-3">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NASA28-16">\n            [16]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Space physics\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA28_16-4">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NASA28-16">\n            [16]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Construction of the\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        (ISS)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Crew rotation and servicing of\n        <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n         Mir\n        </a>\n        and the\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        (ISS)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Servicing missions, such as to repair the\n        <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n         Hubble Space Telescope\n        </a>\n        (HST) and orbiting satellites\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Manned experiments in\n        <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n         low Earth orbit\n        </a>\n        (LEO)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Carried to low Earth orbit (LEO):\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n           Hubble Space Telescope\n          </a>\n          (HST)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Components of the\n          <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n           International Space Station\n          </a>\n          (ISS)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Supplies in\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacehab" title="Spacehab">\n           Spacehab modules\n          </a>\n          or\n          <a href="/wiki/Multi-Purpose_Logistics_Module" title="Multi-Purpose Logistics Module">\n           Multi-Purpose Logistics Modules\n          </a>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Long_Duration_Exposure_Facility" title="Long Duration Exposure Facility">\n           Long Duration Exposure Facility\n          </a>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Upper_Atmosphere_Research_Satellite" title="Upper Atmosphere Research Satellite">\n           Upper Atmosphere Research Satellite\n          </a>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Compton_Gamma_Ray_Observatory" title="Compton Gamma Ray Observatory">\n           Compton Gamma Ray Observatory\n          </a>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          The\n          <a href="/wiki/Earth_Radiation_Budget_Satellite" title="Earth Radiation Budget Satellite">\n           Earth Radiation Budget Satellite\n          </a>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          The Mir Shuttle Docking Node\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Carried satellites with a booster, such as the\n        <a href="/wiki/Payload_Assist_Module" title="Payload Assist Module">\n         Payload Assist Module\n        </a>\n        (PAM-D) or the\n        <a href="/wiki/Inertial_Upper_Stage" title="Inertial Upper Stage">\n         Inertial Upper Stage\n        </a>\n        (IUS), to the point where the booster sends the satellite to:\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          A higher Earth\n          <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n           orbit\n          </a>\n          ; these have included:\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Chandra_X-ray_Observatory" title="Chandra X-ray Observatory">\n             Chandra X-ray Observatory\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            The first six\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TDRS" title="TDRS">\n             TDRS\n            </a>\n            satellites\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            Two DSCS-III (Defense Satellite Communications System) communications satellites in one mission\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            A\n            <a href="/wiki/Defense_Support_Program" title="Defense Support Program">\n             Defense Support Program\n            </a>\n            satellite\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          An interplanetary mission; these have included:\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magellan_probe" title="Magellan probe">\n             <i>\n              Magellan\n             </i>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">\n             <i>\n              Galileo\n             </i>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulysses_probe" title="Ulysses probe">\n             <i>\n              Ulysses\n             </i>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">\n        Budget\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Budget">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1929" data-file-width="3000" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg/220px-Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg/330px-Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg/440px-Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_taking_off_on_STS-27.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         takes flight on the STS-27 mission on December 2, 1988. The Shuttle takes about 8.5 minutes to accelerate to a speed of over 27,000 km/h (17000 mph) and achieve orbit.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="770" data-file-width="1000" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg/220px-950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg/330px-950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg/440px-950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:950318_STS67_Endeavour_landing.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A drag chute is deployed by\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n           Endeavour\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         as it completes a mission of almost 17 days in space on Runway 22 at\n         <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n          Edwards Air Force Base\n         </a>\n         in southern California. Landing occurred at 1:46\xc2\xa0pm (EST), March 18, 1995.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Early during development of the space shuttle, NASA had estimated that the program would cost $7.45\xc2\xa0billion ($43\xc2\xa0billion in 2011 dollars, adjusting for inflation) in development/non-recurring costs, and $9.3M ($54M in 2011 dollars) per flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Early estimates for the cost to deliver payload to low earth orbit were as low as $118 per pound ($260/kg) of payload ($635/lb or $1,400/kg in 2011 dollars), based on marginal or incremental launch costs, and assuming a 65,000 pound (30\xc2\xa0000\xc2\xa0kg) payload capacity and 50 launches per year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-costbenefit_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-costbenefit-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A more realistic projection of 12 flights per year for the 15-year service life combined with the initial development costs would have resulted in a total cost projection for the program of roughly $54\xc2\xa0billion (in 2011 dollars).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The total cost of the actual 30-year service life of the shuttle program through 2011, adjusted for inflation, was $196\xc2\xa0billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_July_2011_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP_July_2011-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The exact breakdown into non-recurring and recurring costs is not available, but, according to NASA, the average cost to launch a Space Shuttle as of 2011 was about $450\xc2\xa0million per mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-missionbudget_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-missionbudget-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Budget" title="NASA Budget">\n        NASA\'s budget\n       </a>\n       for 2005 allocated 30%, or $5\xc2\xa0billion, to space shuttle operations;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_2005_budget_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_2005_budget-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       this was decreased in 2006 to a request of $4.3\xc2\xa0billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_2006_budget_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_2006_budget-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Non-launch costs account for a significant part of the program budget: for example, during fiscal years 2004 to 2006, NASA spent around $13 billion on the space shuttle program,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       even though the fleet was grounded in the aftermath of the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       disaster and there were a total of three launches during this period of time. In fiscal year 2009, NASA budget allocated $2.98\xc2\xa0billion for 5 launches to the program, including $490\xc2\xa0million for "program integration", $1.03\xc2\xa0billion for "flight and ground operations", and $1.46\xc2\xa0billion for "flight hardware" (which includes maintenance of orbiters, engines, and the external tank between flights.)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Per-launch costs can be measured by dividing the total cost over the life of the program (including buildings, facilities, training, salaries, etc.) by the number of launches. With 135 missions, and the total cost of US$192\xc2\xa0billion (in 2010 dollars), this gives approximately $1.5\xc2\xa0billion per launch over the life of the program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pielke_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pielke-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">\n        Accidents\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Accidents">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">\n        <a class="image" class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Challenger_explosion.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         In 1986,\n         <i>\n          Challenger\n         </i>\n         disintegrated one minute and 13 seconds after liftoff.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" href="/wiki/File:Thermal_protection_system_inspections_from_ISS_-_Shuttle_nose.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Discovery\n         </i>\n         as it approaches the International Space Station during\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n          STS-114\n         </a>\n         on July 28, 2005. This was the Shuttle\'s\n         <i>\n          return to flight\n         </i>\n         mission after the Columbia disaster\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the course of 135 missions flown, two orbiters were destroyed, with loss of crew totalling 14 astronauts:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n          Challenger\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 lost 73 seconds after liftoff,\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">\n         STS-51-L\n        </a>\n        , January 28, 1986\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n          Columbia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 lost approximately 16 minutes before its expected landing,\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n         STS-107\n        </a>\n        , February 1, 2003\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Close-up video footage of\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       during its final launch on January 28, 1986 clearly show it began due to an\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        O-ring failure\n       </a>\n       on the right solid rocket booster (SRB). The hot plume of gas leaking from the failed joint caused the collapse of the external tank, which then resulted in the orbiter\'s disintegration due to high aerodynamic stress. The accident resulted in the loss of all seven astronauts on board.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         Endeavour\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (OV-105) was built to replace\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       (using structural spare parts originally intended for the other orbiters) and delivered in May 1991; it was first launched a year later.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the loss of\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       , NASA grounded the shuttle program for over two years, making numerous safety changes recommended by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Commission_Report" title="Rogers Commission Report">\n        Rogers Commission Report\n       </a>\n       , which included a redesign of the SRB joint that failed in the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       accident. Other safety changes included a new escape system for use when the orbiter was in controlled flight, improved landing gear tires and brakes, and the reintroduction of pressure suits for shuttle astronauts (these had been discontinued after\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-4" title="STS-4">\n        STS-4\n       </a>\n       ; astronauts wore only coveralls and oxygen helmets from that point on until the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       accident). The shuttle program continued in September 1988 with the launch of\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-26" title="STS-26">\n        STS-26\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle program operated accident-free for seventeen years after the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       disaster, until\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        broke up on re-entry\n       </a>\n       , killing all seven crew members, on February 1, 2003. The accident began when a piece of foam shed from the external tank struck the leading edge of the orbiter\'s left wing, puncturing one of the reinforced carbon-carbon (RCC) panels that covered the wing edge and protected it during re-entry. As\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       re-entered the atmosphere, hot gas penetrated the wing and destroyed it from the inside out, causing the orbiter to lose control and disintegrate.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA maintains warehoused extensive catalogs of recovered pieces from the two destroyed orbiters.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The accidents did not just affect the technical design of the orbiter, but also NASA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history.nasa.gov_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history.nasa.gov-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Quoting some recommendations made by the post-Challenger Rogers commission:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history.nasa.gov_15-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history.nasa.gov-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <div class="poem">\n        <p>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation I\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 The faulty Solid Rocket Motor joint and seal must be changed. This could be a new design eliminating the joint or a redesign of the current joint and seal. ... the Administrator of NASA should request the National Research Council to form an independent Solid Rocket Motor design oversight committee to implement the Commission\'s design recommendations and oversee the design effort.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation II\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 The Shuttle Program Structure should be reviewed. ... NASA should encourage the transition of qualified astronauts into agency management Positions.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation III\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 NASA and the primary shuttle contractors should review all Criticality 1, 1R, 2, and 2R items and hazard analyses.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation IV\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 NASA should establish an Office of Safety, Reliability and Quality Assurance to be headed by an Associate Administrator, reporting directly to the NASA Administrator.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation VI\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 NASA must take actions to improve landing safety. The tire, brake and nosewheel system must be improved.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation VII\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 Make all efforts to provide a crew escape system for use during controlled gliding flight.\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Recommendation VIII\n         </b>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 The nation\'s reliance on the shuttle as its principal space launch capability created a relentless pressure on NASA to increase the flight rate ... NASA must establish a flight rate that is consistent with its resources.\n        </p>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       After the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       disaster, the International Space Station operated on a skeleton crew of two for more than two years and was serviced primarily by Russian spacecraft. While the "Return to Flight" mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        STS-114\n       </a>\n       in 2005 was successful, a similar piece of foam from a different portion of the tank was shed. Although the debris did not strike\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       , the program was grounded once again for this reason.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The second "Return to Flight" mission,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-121" title="STS-121">\n        STS-121\n       </a>\n       launched on July 4, 2006, at 14:37 (EDT). Two previous launches were scrubbed because of lingering thunderstorms and high winds around the launch pad, and the launch took place despite objections from its chief engineer and safety head. A five-inch (13\xc2\xa0cm) crack in the foam insulation of the external tank gave cause for concern; however, the Mission Management Team gave the go for launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This mission increased the ISS crew to three.\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       touched down successfully on July 17, 2006 at 09:14 (EDT) on Runway 15 at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the success of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-121" title="STS-121">\n        STS-121\n       </a>\n       , all subsequent missions were completed without major foam problems, and the construction of ISS was completed (during the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       mission in August 2007, the orbiter was again struck by a foam fragment on liftoff, but this damage was minimal compared to the damage sustained by\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       Accident Investigation Board, in its report, noted the reduced risk to the crew when a shuttle flew to the International Space Station (ISS), as the station could be used as a safe haven for the crew awaiting rescue in the event that damage to the orbiter on ascent made it unsafe for re-entry. The board recommended that for the remaining flights, the shuttle always orbit with the station. Prior to STS-114, NASA Administrator Sean O\'Keefe declared that all future flights of the shuttle would go to the ISS, precluding the possibility of executing the final\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       servicing mission which had been scheduled before the\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       accident, despite the fact that millions of dollars worth of upgrade equipment for Hubble were ready and waiting in NASA warehouses. Many dissenters, including astronauts\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">\n          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2013)">\n           who?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       , asked NASA management to reconsider allowing the mission, but initially the director stood firm. On October 31, 2006,\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       announced approval of the launch of\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       for the fifth and final shuttle servicing mission to the Hubble Space Telescope, scheduled for August 28, 2008. However SM4/\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       eventually launched in May 2009.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       One impact of\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       was that one the future launch vehicles planned to go into operation after the Shuttle program was concluded, was that\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n        Ares I\n       </a>\n       had a special emphasis on crew safety compared to other considerations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Challenger disaster\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Columbia disaster\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">\n        Retirement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Retirement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2084" data-file-width="3176" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg/220px-STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg/330px-STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg/440px-STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-135_begins_takeoff.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n           Atlantis\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         begins the last mission of the Space Shuttle program\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement" title="Space Shuttle retirement">\n        Space Shuttle retirement\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle program was extended several times beyond its originally envisioned 15-year life span because of the delays in building the United States space station in low Earth orbit \xe2\x80\x93 a project which eventually evolved into the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       . It was formally scheduled for mandatory retirement in 2010 in accord with the directives President George W. Bush issued on January 14, 2004 in his Vision for Space Exploration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bushvision_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bushvision-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A$2.5\xc2\xa0billion spending provision allowing NASA to fly the Space Shuttle beyond its then-scheduled retirement in 2010 passed the Congress in April 2009, although neither NASA nor the White House requested the one-year extension.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The final Space Shuttle launch was that of\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       on July 8, 2011. Although the retirement was planned and roughly in line with what was expected out of STS without further upgrades, the planned replacement for the STS, the Constellation program was cancelled the year before STS concluded. The two programs that took its place, two undetermined commercial crew vehicles and SLS with Orion needed even more time to have a new launcher. NASA has continued to fly to the station via its\n       <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">\n        Roscosmos\n       </a>\n       partner, who still has a functioning manned launcher, the Soyuz system. Manned launch systems have been proposed by other countries, such as the ESA\'s mini-shuttle\n       <a href="/wiki/Hermes_(spacecraft)" title="Hermes (spacecraft)">\n        Hermes\n       </a>\n       launched by an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ariane_rocket" title="Ariane rocket">\n        Ariane rocket\n       </a>\n       , which was cancelled in 1992.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Final_status">\n        Final status\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Final status">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Discovery_@_Udvar_Hazy.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2944" data-file-width="3805" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png/220px-Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png/330px-Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png/440px-Space_Shuttle_Discovery_%40_Udvar_Hazy.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Discovery_@_Udvar_Hazy.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle Discovery at the Udvar Hazy museum\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Out of the five fully functional shuttle orbiters built, three remain.\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       , which was used for atmospheric test flights but not for orbital flight, had many parts taken out for use on the other orbiters. It was later visually restored and was on display at the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">\n        National Air and Space Museum\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center">\n        Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center\n       </a>\n       until April 19, 2012.\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       was moved to New York City in April 2012 to be displayed at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intrepid_Sea,_Air_%26_Space_Museum" title="Intrepid Sea, Air &amp; Space Museum">\n        Intrepid Sea, Air &amp; Space Museum\n       </a>\n       , whose Space Shuttle Pavilion opened on July 19, 2012.\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       replaced\n       <i>\n        Enterprise\n       </i>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">\n        National Air and Space Museum\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center">\n        Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center\n       </a>\n       .\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       formed part of the Space Shuttle Exhibit at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       visitor complex and has been on display there since June 29, 2013 following its refurbishment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On October 14, 2012,\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       completed an unprecedented 12\xc2\xa0mi (19\xc2\xa0km) drive on city streets from\n       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">\n        Los Angeles International Airport\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/California_Science_Center" title="California Science Center">\n        California Science Center\n       </a>\n       , where it has been on display in a temporary hangar since late 2012. The transport from the airport took two days and required major street closures, the removal of over 400 city trees, and extensive work to raise power lines, level the street, and temporarily remove street signs, lamp posts, and other obstacles. Hundreds of volunteers, and fire and police personnel, helped with the transport. Large crowds of spectators waited on the streets to see the shuttle as it passed through the city.\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       will be displayed permanently beginning in 2017 at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Oschin" title="Samuel Oschin">\n        Samuel Oschin\n       </a>\n       Air and Space Center (an addition to the California Science Center currently under construction), where it will be mounted in the vertical position complete with solid rocket boosters and an external tank.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casc_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-casc-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_modules">\n        Passenger modules\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Passenger modules">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table <small>\n          \xe2\x80\x94 host\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spacehab_S107e05359.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Spacehab module\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crewmembers_of_STS-71,_Mir-18_and_Mir-19_Pose_for_Inflight_Picture_-_GPN-2002-000061_rotated.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3352" data-file-width="5184" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Crewmembers_of_STS-71%2C_Mir-18_and_Mir-19_Pose_for_Inflight_Picture_-_GPN-2002-000061_rotated.jpg/220px-Crewmembers_of_STS-71%2C_Mir-18_and_Mir-19_Pose_for_Inflight_Picture_-_GPN-2002-000061_rotated.jpg"
