2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crewmembers_of_STS-71,_Mir-18_and_Mir-19_Pose_for_Inflight_Picture_-_GPN-2002-000061_rotated.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ten people inside Spacelab Module in the Shuttle bay in June 1995, celebrating the docking of the Space Shuttle and Mir.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       One area of Space Shuttle applications is an expanded crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orbiter_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-orbiter-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Crews of up to 8 have been flown in the Orbiter, but it could have held at least a crew of ten.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orbiter_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-orbiter-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Various proposals for filling the payload bay with additional passengers were also made as early as 1979.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reichert_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-reichert-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One proposal by\n       <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_International" title="Rockwell International">\n        Rockwell\n       </a>\n       provided seating for 74 passengers in the Orbiter payload bay, with support for three days in Earth orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reichert_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-reichert-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With a smaller 64 seat orbiter, costs for the late 1980s would be around 1.5\xc2\xa0million USD per seat per launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-david_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-david-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Rockwell passenger module had two decks, 4 seats across on top and 2 on the bottom, including a 25-inch (63.5\xc2\xa0cm) wide isle and extra storage space.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-david_33-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-david-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another design was Space Habitation Design Associates 1983 proposal for 72 passengers in the Space Shuttle Payload bay.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-david_33-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-david-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Passengers were located in 6 sections, each with windows and its own loading ramp at launch, and with seats in different configurations for launch and landing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-david_33-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-david-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another proposal was based on the Spacelab habitation modules, which provided 32 seats in the payload bay in addition to those in the cockpit area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-david_33-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-david-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were some efforts to analyze commercial operation of STS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Using the NASA figure for average cost to launch a Space Shuttle as of 2011 at about $450\xc2\xa0million per mission,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-missionbudget_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-missionbudget-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a cost per seat for a 74\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launiusr.files.wordpress.com_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-launiusr.files.wordpress.com-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       seat module envisioned by Rockwell came to less than $6\xc2\xa0million, not including the regular crew. Some passenger modules used hardware similar to existing equipment, such as the tunnel,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launiusr.files.wordpress.com_36-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-launiusr.files.wordpress.com-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which was also needed for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacehab" title="Spacehab">\n        Spacehab\n       </a>\n       and Spacelab\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Space_Shuttle_crews" title="List of Space Shuttle crews">\n        List of Space Shuttle crews\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Successors">\n        Successors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Successors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2361" data-file-width="3000" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg/220px-Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg/330px-Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg/440px-Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Twin_Linear_Aerospike_XRS-2200_Engine_PLW_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Linear aerospike engine for the cancelled X-33\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COTS2Dragon.2..jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1016" data-file-width="1158" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/COTS2Dragon.2..jpg/220px-COTS2Dragon.2..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/COTS2Dragon.2..jpg/330px-COTS2Dragon.2..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/COTS2Dragon.2..jpg/440px-COTS2Dragon.2..jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COTS2Dragon.2..jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Dragon spacecraft, one of the Space Shuttle\'s several successors, is seen here on its way to deliver cargo to the ISS\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="4267" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/220px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/330px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/440px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Vision for the developmental Orion spacecraft\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg/220px-Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg/330px-Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg/440px-Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_at_Launch_Pad_39B_sunrise.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ares I test\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the three decades of operation, various follow-on and replacements for the STS Space Shuttle were partially developed but not finished.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Examples of possible future space vehicles to supplement or supplant STS:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        National Aero-Space Plane (NASP)\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_X-30" title="Rockwell X-30">\n           Rockwell X-30\n          </a>\n          (not funded)\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_X-33" title="Lockheed Martin X-33">\n         Lockheed Martin X-33\n        </a>\n        (cancelled 2001)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n         Ares I\n        </a>\n        (ended with Constellation cancellation)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Space_Plane_Program" title="Orbital Space Plane Program">\n         Orbital Space Plane Program\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       One effort in the direction of space transportation was the Reusable Launch Vehicle (RLV) program, initiated in 1994 by NASA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinoff.nasa.gov_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spinoff.nasa.gov-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This led to work on the X-33 and X-34 vehicles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinoff.nasa.gov_38-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spinoff.nasa.gov-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA spent about 1\xc2\xa0billion USD on developing the X-33 hoping for it be in operation by 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinoff.nasa.gov_38-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spinoff.nasa.gov-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another program around the turn of the millennium was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_Initiative" title="Space Launch Initiative">\n        Space Launch Initiative\n       </a>\n       , which was a next generation launch initaive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.gov_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa.gov-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Space Launch Initiative program was started in 2001, and in late 2002 it was evolved into two programs, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Space_Plane_Program" title="Orbital Space Plane Program">\n        Orbital Space Plane Program\n       </a>\n       and the Next Generation Launch Technology program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.gov_39-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa.gov-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       OSP was oriented towards provided access to the International Space Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa.gov_39-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa.gov-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other vehicles that would have taken over some of the Shuttles responsibilities were the\n       <a href="/wiki/HL-20_Personnel_Launch_System" title="HL-20 Personnel Launch System">\n        HL-20 Personnel Launch System\n       </a>\n       or the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_X-38" title="NASA X-38">\n        NASA X-38\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Crew_Return_Vehicle" title="Crew Return Vehicle">\n        Crew Return Vehicle\n       </a>\n       program, which were primarily for getting people down from ISS. The X-38 was cancelled in 2002,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the HL-20 was cancelled in 1993.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several other programs in this existed such as the Station Crew Return Alternative Module (SCRAM) and Assured Crew Return Vehicle (ACRV)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the 2004 Vision for Space Exploration, the next manned NASA program was to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Constellation" title="Project Constellation">\n        Project Constellation\n       </a>\n       with its\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n        Ares I\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_V" title="Ares V">\n        Ares V\n       </a>\n       launch vehicles and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Spacecraft" title="Orion Spacecraft">\n        Orion Spacecraft\n       </a>\n       ; however, the Constellation program was never fully funded, and in early 2010 the Obama administration asked Congress to instead endorse a plan with heavy reliance on the private sector for delivering cargo and crew to LEO.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n       (COTS) program began in 2006 with the purpose of creating commercially operated unmanned cargo vehicles to service the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first of these vehicles,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon\n       </a>\n       , became operational in 2012, and the second,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences" title="Orbital Sciences">\n        Orbital Sciences\n       </a>\n       \'\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">\n        Cygnus\n       </a>\n       did so in 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development\n       </a>\n       (CCDev) program was initiated in 2010 with the purpose of creating commercially operated manned spacecraft capable of delivering at least four crew members to the ISS, staying docked for 180 days and then returning them back to Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These spacecraft, like the SpaceX\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_V2" title="Dragon V2">\n        Dragon V2\n       </a>\n       and Sierra Nevada Corporation\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chaser" title="Dream Chaser">\n        Dream Chaser\n       </a>\n       are expected to become operational around 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the Constellation program was canceled, it has been replaced with a very similar beyond low Earth orbit program. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" title="Orion spacecraft">\n        Orion spacecraft\n       </a>\n       has been left virtually unchanged from its previous design. The planned\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_V" title="Ares V">\n        Ares V\n       </a>\n       rocket has been replaced with the smaller\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       (SLS), which is planned to launch both Orion and other necessary hardware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Flight_Test_1" title="Exploration Flight Test 1">\n        Exploration Flight Test-1\n       </a>\n       (EFT-1), an unmanned test flight of the Orion spacecraft, launched on December 5, 2014 on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">\n        Delta IV Heavy\n       </a>\n       rocket.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schedule-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">\n        Exploration Mission-1\n       </a>\n       (EM-1) is the unmanned initial launch of the SLS, which is planned for 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schedule-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Exploration Mission-2 (EM-2) is the first manned flight of Orion and SLS and is scheduled for 2019.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_48-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schedule-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       EM-2 is a 10-14-day mission planned to place a crew of four into Lunar orbit. As of September 2013\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the destination for EM-3 and immediate destination focus for this new program is still in-flux.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement" title="Space Shuttle retirement">\n        Space Shuttle retirement\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Assets_and_transition_plan">\n        Assets and transition plan\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Assets and transition plan">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="905" data-file-width="1680" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png/250px-STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png/375px-STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png/500px-STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-135_30_mins_after_touchdown2.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         about 30 minutes after final touchdown\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle program occupied over 654 facilities, used over 1.2\xc2\xa0million line items of equipment, and employed over 5,000 people. The total value of equipment was over $12\xc2\xa0billion. Shuttle-related facilities represented over a quarter of NASA\'s inventory. There were over 1,200 active suppliers to the program throughout the United States. NASA\'s transition plan had the program operating through 2010 with a transition and retirement phase lasting through 2015. During this time, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n        Ares I\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       as well as the Altair Lunar Lander were to be under development,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTMP_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NTMP-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       although these programs have since been canceled.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Critiques">\n        Critiques\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critiques">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_Space_Shuttle_program" title="Criticism of the Space Shuttle program">\n        Criticism of the Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle program has been criticized for failing to achieve its promised cost and utility goals, as well as design, cost, management, and safety issues.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Others have argued that the Shuttle program was a step backwards from the Apollo Program, which, while extremely dangerous, accomplished far more scientific and space exploration endeavors than the Shuttle ever could.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       , high-profile boards convened to investigate the accidents with both committees returning praise and serious critiques to the program and NASA management. Some of the most famous of the criticisms, most of management, came from Nobel Prize winner\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Feynman" title="Richard Feynman">\n        Richard Feynman\n       </a>\n       , in his report that followed his\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rogers_Commission#Role_of_Richard_Feynman" title="Rogers Commission">\n        appointment to the commission\n       </a>\n       responsible for investigating the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       disaster.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commission_report_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Commission_report-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Support_vehicles">\n        Support vehicles\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Space_Shuttle_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Support vehicles">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crawler-Transporter.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1993" data-file-width="3000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/220px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/330px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/440px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crawler-Transporter.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Crawler-transporter No.2 ("Franz") in a December 2004 road test after track shoe replacement\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2372" data-file-width="3030" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg/220px-Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg/330px-Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg/440px-Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shuttle_mate_demate_facility.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         being prepared to be mated to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Carrier_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Carrier Aircraft">\n          Shuttle Carrier Aircraft\n         </a>\n         using the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mate-Demate_Device" title="Mate-Demate Device">\n          Mate-Demate Device\n         </a>\n         following\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-44" title="STS-44">\n          STS-44\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Many other vehicles were used in support of the Space Shuttle program, mainly terrestrial transportation vehicles.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crawler-Transporter" title="Crawler-Transporter">\n         Crawler-Transporter\n        </a>\n        carried the\n        <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Launcher_Platform" title="Mobile Launcher Platform">\n         Mobile Launcher Platform\n        </a>\n        and the space shuttle from the\n        <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n         Vehicle Assembly Building\n        </a>\n        (VAB) to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Launch_Complex_39" title="Launch Complex 39">\n         Launch Complex\xc2\xa039\n        </a>\n        , originally built for Project Apollo.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Carrier_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Carrier Aircraft">\n         Shuttle Carrier Aircraft\n        </a>\n        (SCA) were two modified\n        <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">\n         Boeing 747s\n        </a>\n        . Either could fly an orbiter from alternative landing sites back to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n         Kennedy Space Center\n        </a>\n        . These aircraft were retired to the\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joe_Davies_Heritage_Airpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joe Davies Heritage Airpark (page does not exist)">\n         Joe Davies Heritage Airpark\n        </a>\n        at the\n        <a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Flight_Research_Center" title="Armstrong Flight Research Center">\n         Armstrong Flight Research Center\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Center_Houston" title="Space Center Houston">\n         Space Center Houston\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A 36-wheeled transport trailer, the Orbiter Transfer System, originally built for the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force">\n         U.S. Air Force\n        </a>\n        \'s launch facility at\n        <a href="/wiki/Vandenberg_Air_Force_Base" title="Vandenberg Air Force Base">\n         Vandenberg Air Force Base\n        </a>\n        in California (since then converted for\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delta_IV_rocket" title="Delta IV rocket">\n         Delta\xc2\xa0IV rockets\n        </a>\n        ) would transport the orbiter from the landing facility to the launch pad, which allowed both "stacking" and launch without utilizing a separate VAB-style building and crawler-transporter roadway. Prior to the closing of the Vandenberg facility, orbiters were transported from the\n        <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n         OPF\n        </a>\n        to the VAB on their undercarriages, only to be raised when the orbiter was being lifted for attachment to the SRB/ET stack. The trailer allowed the transportation of the orbiter from the OPF to either the SCA\n        <a href="/wiki/Mate-Demate_Device" title="Mate-Demate Device">\n         "Mate-Demate"\n        </a>\n        stand or the VAB without placing any additional stress on the undercarriage.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Mobile_lounge#Crew_Transport_Vehicle_.28NASA.29" title="Mobile lounge">\n         Crew Transport Vehicle\n        </a>\n        (CTV), a modified airport\n        <a href="/wiki/Mobile_lounge" title="Mobile lounge">\n         jet bridge\n        </a>\n        , was used to assist astronauts to egress from the orbiter after landing. Upon entering the CTV, astronauts could take off their launch and re-entry suits then proceed to chairs and beds for medical checks before being transported back to the crew quarters in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n         Operations and Checkout Building\n        </a>\n        . Originally built for Project Apollo.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_transfer_van" title="Astronaut transfer van">\n         Astrovan\n        </a>\n        was used to transport astronauts from the crew quarters in the Operations and Checkout Building to the launch pad on launch day. It was also used to transport astronauts back again from the Crew Transport Vehicle at the\n        <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n         Shuttle Landing Facility\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The three locomotives serving the\n        <a href="/wiki/NASA_Railroad" title="NASA Railroad">\n         NASA Railroad\n        </a>\n        , used to transport segments of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n         Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Boosters\n        </a>\n        , were determined to be no longer needed for day-to-day operation at the Kennedy Space Center. In April 2015, locomotive No. 1 was sent to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natchitoches_Parish_Port" title="Natchitoches Parish Port">\n         Natchitoches Parish Port\n        </a>\n        and No. 3 sent to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Madison_Railroad" title="Madison Railroad">\n         Madison Railroad\n        </a>\n        . Locomotive No. 2 was sent to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_Railroad_Museum" title="Gold Coast Railroad Museum">\n         Gold Coast Railroad Museum\n        </a>\n        in 2014.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n         <a href="#cite_note-53">\n          [53]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline"
